We might eventually be able to relax this\n\t * restriction, but for now it seems best not to have parallel workers\n\t * trying to create their own parallel workers.\n\t */\n\tif ((cursorOptions & CURSOR_OPT_PARALLEL_OK) != 0 &&\n\t\tIsUnderPostmaster &&\n\t\tparse->commandType == CMD_SELECT &&\n\t\t!parse->hasModifyingCTE &&\n\t\tmax_parallel_workers_per_gather > 0 &&\n\t\t!IsParallelWorker())\n\t{\n\t\t/* all the cheap tests pass, so scan the query tree */\n\t\tglob->maxParallelHazard = max_parallel_hazard(parse);\n\t\tglob->parallelModeOK = (glob->maxParallelHazard != PROPARALLEL_UNSAFE);\n\t}\n\telse\n\t{\n\t\t/* skip the query tree scan, just assume it's unsafe */\n\t\tglob->maxParallelHazard = PROPARALLEL_UNSAFE;\n\t\tglob->parallelModeOK = false;\n\t}\n\n\t/*\n\t * glob->parallelModeNeeded is normally set to false here and changed to\n\t * true during plan creation if a Gather or Gather Merge plan is actually\n\t * created (cf. create_gather_plan, create_gather_merge_plan).\n\t *\n\t * However, if debug_parallel_query = on or debug_parallel_query =\n\t * regress, then we impose parallel mode whenever it's safe to do so, even\n\t * if the final plan doesn't use parallelism.  It's not safe to do so if\n\t * the query contains anything parallel-unsafe; parallelModeOK will be\n\t * false in that case.  Note that parallelModeOK can't change after this\n\t * point. Otherwise, everything in the query is either parallel-safe or\n\t * parallel-restricted, and in either case it should be OK to impose\n\t * parallel-mode restrictions.  If that ends up breaking something, then\n\t * either some function the user included in the query is incorrectly\n\t * labeled as parallel-safe or parallel-restricted when in reality it's\n\t * parallel-unsafe, or else the query planner itself has a bug.\n\t */\n\tglob->parallelModeNeeded = glob->parallelModeOK &&\n\t\t(debug_parallel_query != DEBUG_PARALLEL_OFF);\n\n\t/* Determine what fraction of the plan is likely to be scanned */\n\tif (cursorOptions & CURSOR_OPT_FAST_PLAN)\n\t{\n\t\t/*\n\t\t * We have no real idea how many tuples the user will ultimately FETCH\n\t\t * from a cursor, but it is often the case that he doesn't want 'em\n\t\t * all, or would prefer a fast-start plan anyway so that he can\n\t\t * process some of the tuples sooner.  Use a GUC parameter to decide\n\t\t * what fraction to optimize for.\n\t\t */\n\t\ttuple_fraction = cursor_tuple_fraction;\n\n\t\t/*\n\t\t * We document cursor_tuple_fraction as simply being a fraction, which\n\t\t * means the edge cases 0 and 1 have to be treated specially here.  We\n\t\t * convert 1 to 0 (\"all the tuples\") and 0 to a very small fraction.\n\t\t */\n\t\tif (tuple_fraction >= 1.0)\n\t\t\ttuple_fraction = 0.0;\n\t\telse if (tuple_fraction <= 0.0)\n\t\t\ttuple_fraction = 1e-10;\n\t}\n\telse\n\t{\n\t\t/* Default assumption is we need all the tuples */\n\t\ttuple_fraction = 0.0;\n\t}\n\n\t/* primary planning entry point (may recurse for subqueries) */\n\troot = subquery_planner(glob, parse, NULL, false, tuple_fraction, NULL);","numLines":150,"startLine":286,"totalLines":8339}}}

pointer `node->ExecProcNode` (set by `ExecSetExecProcNode()`) — calls the node-specific function\n   - Node-specific functions (e.g. `ExecSeqScan`, `ExecNestLoop`) recursively call `ExecProcNode()` on child nodes\n   - Returns `NULL` slot to signal end-of-stream\n\n9. **Cleanup**: `ExecutorFinish()` then `ExecutorEnd()` → `ExecEndNode()` recursively cleans up\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n**1. Pipeline / Stage Architecture**\nThe query pipeline is a strict linear sequence of transformations, each consuming the output of the prior stage. The stages are cleanly separated: raw parsing has no catalog access (safe in aborted transactions), semantic analysis acquires catalog locks, the rewriter applies declarative rules, the optimizer generates a cost-optimal plan, and the executor runs it. This separation enables features like prepared statements (parse once, plan many times) and `EXPLAIN` (run all stages but skip execution).\n\n**2. Tagged Union Node System (NodeTag dispatch)**\nAll major data structures — parse tree nodes, plan nodes, executor state nodes — embed a `NodeTag` as their first field and are cast to/from base types via C-level polymorphism. The `nodeTag()` macro reads this tag, and all major dispatch functions (`ExecInitNode`, `ExecEndNode`, `create_plan_recurse`, `ExecProcNode`) use a `switch(nodeTag(node))` to dispatch to the correct specialized function. This is a C implementation of virtual dispatch without vtables.\n\n**3. Volcano / Iterator Executor Model**\nThe executor implements the classic Volcano (Graefe, 1994) pull-based iterator model. Every plan node implements three operations: `Init` (open), `GetTuple` (next), and `End` (close). The top node is driven by a loop in `ExecutePlan()` calling `ExecProcNode()` repeatedly. Each node calls `ExecProcNode()` on its children as needed. This creates a demand-driven pipeline: tuples are not materialized unless a blocking node (Sort, Hash) requires it. The function pointer `node->ExecProcNode` (set in `PlanState`) enables zero-overhead dispatch after the first call installs the real function (replacing `ExecProcNodeFirst`).\n\n**4. Two-Phase Optimization (Path/Plan separation)**\nThe optimizer uses a strict two-phase design:\n\n- **Phase 1 — Path generation** (`allpaths.c`, `joinpath.c`, `pathnode.c`, `costsize.c`): Explores the full space of physical access strategies. Each `RelOptInfo` (representing a base table or join) accumulates a list of `Path` nodes — one per strategy (SeqScan, IndexScan, BitmapScan, NestLoop, MergeJoin, HashJoin, etc.). Each Path has startup and total cost estimates. The cheapest paths are retained via `add_path()`. This is a dynamic-programming approach: join paths for N relations are built from cheaper sub-join paths.\n\n- **Phase 2 — Plan creation** (`createplan.c`): Once the optimizer selects the best Path (cheapest cost for the desired `tuple_fraction`), `create_plan()` recursively walks the Path tree and instantiates concrete `Plan` nodes. Plan nodes are executor-facing structures that reference Vars by relation-column offsets rather than catalog OIDs.\n\n**5. Hook Architecture**\nThe pipeline has hook points at every major stage: `post_parse_analyze_hook`, `planner_hook`, `set_rel_pathlist_hook`, `join_search_hook`, `create_upper_paths_hook`, `ExecutorStart_hook`, `ExecutorRun_hook`, `ExecutorFinish_hook`, `ExecutorEnd_hook`. These allow extensions (pg_stat_statements, auto_explain, custom access methods) to intercept and augment each stage without modifying core code.\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Input | Output | Key Responsibility |\n|-----------|-------|--------|--------------------|\n| `parser.c` + `scan.l` + `gram.y` | SQL string | `List<RawStmt>` | Lexing and grammar; no catalog access |\n| `analyze.c` | `RawStmt` | `Query` | Name resolution, type checking, semantic validation |\n| `rewriteHandler.c` | `Query` | `List<Query>` | View expansion, rule application, RLS |\n| `planner.c` / `allpaths.c` | `Query` | `Path` tree | Cost-based optimization, path enumeration |\n| `createplan.c` | `Path` | `Plan` tree | Path → executor-ready Plan conversion |\n| `execMain.c` | `PlannedStmt` | tuples | Executor lifecycle management |\n| `execProcnode.c` | `Plan` / `PlanState` | `TupleTableSlot` | Volcano dispatch |\n\n### Data Flow / Type Transformations\n\n```\nSQL string (const char*)\n    ↓ raw_parser() [parser.c + scan.l + gram.y]\nList<RawStmt>          — raw AST, no semantic content\n    ↓ parse_analyze_fixedparams() [analyze.c]\nQuery                  — semantic query tree: rtable, jointree, targetList, qualifications\n    ↓ QueryRewrite() [rewriteHandler.c]\nList<Query>            — post-rewrite queries (views expanded, rules applied)\n    ↓ planner() [planner.c] → make_one_rel() [allpaths.c]  [Phase 1]\nRelOptInfo with Path list — cost-annotated access strategy alternatives\n    ↓ create_plan() [createplan.c]                          [Phase 2]\nPlannedStmt { Plan *planTree } — executable plan tree\n    ↓ ExecutorStart() [execMain.c] → ExecInitNode() [execProcnode.c]\nPlanState tree         — runtime state parallel to Plan tree\n    ↓ ExecutorRun() → ExecutePlan() → ExecProcNode() loop [execProcnode.c]\nTupleTableSlot*        — one tuple per call (NULL = done)\n    ↓ DestReceiver.receiveSlot()\nClient result rows\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n- `RawStmt` has no OID references; it is safe to construct without catalog access\n- `Query` holds table/column names resolved to `Var` nodes with `varno` (range table index) and `varattno` (attribute number)\n- `PlannedStmt.planTree` is a tree of `Plan` nodes where all Vars are resolved to executor attribute numbers via `setrefs.c`\n- `PlanState` nodes are allocated 1:1 with `Plan` nodes and hold mutable execution state (current tuple, scan state, hash table, etc.)\n- `TupleTableSlot` is a fixed-size descriptor pointing to either a heap tuple or a virtual tuple of Datums; returned by reference and valid only until the next `ExecProcNode()` call unless explicitly copied\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL's query execution pipeline transforms a SQL string through five distinct stages: (1) **Parsing** (`parser.c`/`scan.l`/`gram.y`) produces a raw AST (`RawStmt`) with no catalog access; (2) **Semantic analysis** (`analyze.c`) resolves names and types to produce a `Query` node; (3) **Rewriting** (`rewriteHandler.c`) expands views and applies rules, yielding a `List<Query>`; (4) **Optimization** uses a two-phase process — path enumeration (`allpaths.c`) explores all access strategies with cost estimation, then `create_plan()` (`createplan.c`) converts the cheapest `Path` tree into an executable `PlannedStmt`; (5) **Execution** (`execMain.c`, `execProcnode.c`) uses the Volcano iterator model where `ExecProcNode()` dispatches via a per-node function pointer to node-specific handlers that recursively pull tuples from child nodes until `NULL` signals end-of-stream. The entire pipeline is extensible via hook points at each stage boundary.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1937,"cache_read_input_tokens":66077,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1937,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":18,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b1678ded-9d05-4f65-8560-eb9ecd6742c3","uuid":"56a04526-dd01-4799-a58a-ef718047ee5c"}

`src/backend/rewrite/rewriteHandler.c` — primary rewrite engine; `QueryRewrite()` applies rules, `RewriteQuery()` for non-SELECT rules, `fireRIRrules()` for SELECT rules\n- `src/backend/rewrite/rewriteDefine.c` — rule definition storage\n- `src/backend/rewrite/rowsecurity.c` — row-level security policy application\n\n### Optimizer / Planner\n- `src/backend/optimizer/plan/planner.c` — top-level planner interface; `planner()` → `standard_planner()` → `subquery_planner()` → `grouping_planner()`\n- `src/backend/optimizer/plan/planmain.c` — core join planning; `query_planner()` drives path generation for basic joins\n- `src/backend/optimizer/path/allpaths.c` — **Phase 1 (Path generation)**; `make_one_rel()` → `set_base_rel_pathlists()` + `make_rel_from_joinlist()`; enumerates all access and join paths\n- `src/backend/optimizer/path/joinpath.c` — join path generation (NestLoop, MergeJoin, HashJoin)\n- `src/backend/optimizer/path/joinrels.c` — join relation construction and dynamic programming\n- `src/backend/optimizer/path/indxpath.c` — index scan path generation\n- `src/backend/optimizer/path/costsize.c` — cost estimation for all path types\n- `src/backend/optimizer/path/equivclass.c` — equivalence class management for join predicates\n- `src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c` — **Phase 2 (Plan creation)**; `create_plan()` → `create_plan_recurse()` converts cheapest Path → executable Plan nodes\n- `src/backend/optimizer/plan/setrefs.c` — final variable resolution pass after plan creation\n- `src/backend/optimizer/plan/initsplan.c` — initial plan setup, restriction clause processing\n- `src/backend/optimizer/plan/subselect.c` — subquery planning and parameterization\n- `src/backend/optimizer/prep/prepjointree.c` — join tree preprocessing (subquery flattening)\n- `src/backend/optimizer/prep/prepqual.c` — qualification preprocessing\n- `src/backend/optimizer/util/pathnode.c` — path node creation utilities; `add_path()` to maintain cheapest path lists\n- `src/backend/optimizer/util/relnode.c` — RelOptInfo node construction\n- `src/backend/optimizer/util/plancat.c` — catalog access for planner statistics\n- `src/backend/optimizer/geqo/geqo_main.c` — Genetic Query Optimizer for large join counts\n- `src/backend/optimizer/path/clausesel.c` — selectivity estimation for clauses\n\n### Executor\n- `src/backend/executor/execMain.c` — executor top-level interface; `ExecutorStart()`, `ExecutorRun()`, `ExecutorFinish()`, `ExecutorEnd()`\n- `src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c` — **Volcano-model dispatch**; `ExecInitNode()`, `ExecProcNode()` (via function pointer), `ExecEndNode()`\n- `src/backend/executor/execScan.c` — generic scan loop shared by scan nodes\n- `src/backend/executor/execExpr.c` / `execExprInterp.c` — expression evaluation engine (JIT-compilable)\n- `src/backend/executor/execTuples.c` — tuple slot management (TupleTableSlot)\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeSeqscan.c` — sequential heap scan\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeIndexscan.c` — index scan\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeNestloop.c` — nested-loop join\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeHashjoin.c` — hash join\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeMergejoin.c` — merge join\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeAgg.c` — aggregation\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeSort.c` — sort\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeModifyTable.c` — INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE/MERGE execution\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeHash.c` — hash table construction (for HashJoin)\n- `src/backend/executor/nodeLimit.c` — LIMIT/OFFSET handling\n- `src/backend/executor/execParallel.c` — parallel query worker coordination\n\n### Node Type Definitions\n- `src/include/nodes/parsenodes.h` — `RawStmt`, `Query` structs (parser output)\n- `src/include/nodes/plannodes.h` — `PlannedStmt`, `Plan` and all plan node structs\n- `src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h` — `PlannerInfo`, `RelOptInfo`, `Path` and all path node structs\n- `src/include/nodes/execnodes.h` — `EState`, `PlanState`, `TupleTableSlot` and all executor state structs\n- `src/include/nodes/primnodes.h` — primitive expression nodes (Var, Const, FuncExpr, etc.)\n- `src/include/nodes/nodes.h` — NodeTag enum (all node type identifiers)\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Entry point**: `src/backend/tcop/postgres.c:exec_simple_query()`\n   - Receives raw SQL string from client protocol message\n\n2. **Lexing + Parsing**: calls `pg_parse_query()` (same file)\n   - Calls `raw_parser()` in `src/backend/parser/parser.c`\n   - `raw_parser()` initializes flex scanner (`scanner_init()` from `scan.l`) and bison parser (`base_yyparse()` from `gram.y`)\n   - Returns `List *` of `RawStmt` nodes — raw, unvalidated AST\n\n3. **Semantic Analysis**: calls `pg_analyze_and_rewrite_fixedparams()` (same file)\n   - Calls `parse_analyze_fixedparams()` in `src/backend/parser/analyze.c`\n   - `analyze.c` dispatches to `transformSelectStmt()`, `transformInsertStmt()`, etc.\n   - Resolves table/column names against catalog, checks types, resolves operators and functions\n   - Returns single `Query *` node — semantically validated query tree\n\n4. **Query Rewriting**: calls `pg_rewrite_query()` (same file)\n   - Calls `QueryRewrite()` in `src/backend/rewrite/rewriteHandler.c`\n   - Applies user-defined rewrite rules (views expand here via `fireRIRrules()`)\n   - Applies row-level security policies\n   - Returns `List *` of `Query *` nodes (one query may expand to several)\n\n5. **Planning/Optimization**: calls `pg_plan_queries()` → `pg_plan_query()` (same file)\n   - Calls `planner()` in `src/backend/optimizer/plan/planner.c`\n   - `planner()` checks for `planner_hook`, else calls `standard_planner()`\n   - `standard_planner()` calls `subquery_planner()` which calls `grouping_planner()`\n   - `grouping_planner()` calls `query_planner()` in `src/backend/optimizer/plan/planmain.c`\n   - `query_planner()` calls `make_one_rel()` in `src/backend/optimizer/path/allpaths.c` — **Path generation phase**\n   - `standard_planner()` then calls `create_plan()` in `src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c` — **Plan creation phase**\n   - Returns `PlannedStmt *` — executable plan tree\n\n6. **Portal setup**: back in `exec_simple_query()`\n   - Creates a `Portal` with `CreatePortal()` / `PortalDefineQuery()` / `PortalStart()`\n   - Calls `PortalRun()` in `src/backend/tcop/pquery.c`\n\n7. **Execution dispatch**: `PortalRun()` → `PortalRunMulti()` → `ProcessQuery()`\n   - `ProcessQuery()` calls `CreateQueryDesc()` to wrap the `PlannedStmt`\n   - Calls `ExecutorStart()` in `src/backend/executor/execMain.c`\n   - `ExecutorStart()` → `standard_ExecutorStart()` creates `EState` and calls `InitPlan()` which calls `ExecInitNode()` in `src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c`\n   - Calls `ExecutorRun()` → `ExecutePlan()` which loops calling `ExecProcNode()` on the root node\n   - Each `ExecProcNode()` call returns a `TupleTableSlot *` (one tuple at a time)\n\n8. **Volcano dispatch loop**: `ExecProcNode()` in `src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c`\n   - Uses function pointer `node->ExecProcNode` (set by `ExecSetExecProcNode()`) — calls the node-specific function\n   - Node-specific functions (e.g. `ExecSeqScan`, `ExecNestLoop`) recursively call `ExecProcNode()` on child nodes\n   - Returns `NULL` slot to signal end-of-stream\n\n9. **Cleanup**: `ExecutorFinish()` then `ExecutorEnd()` → `ExecEndNode()` recursively cleans up\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n**1. Pipeline / Stage Architecture**\nThe query pipeline is a strict linear sequence of transformations, each consuming the output of the prior stage. The stages are cleanly separated: raw parsing has no catalog access (safe in aborted transactions), semantic analysis acquires catalog locks, the rewriter applies declarative rules, the optimizer generates a cost-optimal plan, and the executor runs it. This separation enables features like prepared statements (parse once, plan many times) and `EXPLAIN` (run all stages but skip execution).\n\n**2. Tagged Union Node System (NodeTag dispatch)**\nAll major data structures — parse tree nodes, plan nodes, executor state nodes — embed a `NodeTag` as their first field and are cast to/from base types via C-level polymorphism. The `nodeTag()` macro reads this tag, and all major dispatch functions (`ExecInitNode`, `ExecEndNode`, `create_plan_recurse`, `ExecProcNode`) use a `switch(nodeTag(node))` to dispatch to the correct specialized function. This is a C implementation of virtual dispatch without vtables.\n\n**3. Volcano / Iterator Executor Model**\nThe executor implements the classic Volcano (Graefe, 1994) pull-based iterator model. Every plan node implements three operations: `Init` (open), `GetTuple` (next), and `End` (close). The top node is driven by a loop in `ExecutePlan()` calling `ExecProcNode()` repeatedly. Each node calls `ExecProcNode()` on its children as needed. This creates a demand-driven pipeline: tuples are not materialized unless a blocking node (Sort, Hash) requires it. The function pointer `node->ExecProcNode` (set in `PlanState`) enables zero-overhead dispatch after the first call installs the real function (replacing `ExecProcNodeFirst`).\n\n**4. Two-Phase Optimization (Path/Plan separation)**\nThe optimizer uses a strict two-phase design:\n\n- **Phase 1 — Path generation** (`allpaths.c`, `joinpath.c`, `pathnode.c`, `costsize.c`): Explores the full space of physical access strategies. Each `RelOptInfo` (representing a base table or join) accumulates a list of `Path` nodes — one per strategy (SeqScan, IndexScan, BitmapScan, NestLoop, MergeJoin, HashJoin, etc.). Each Path has startup and total cost estimates. The cheapest paths are retained via `add_path()`. This is a dynamic-programming approach: join paths for N relations are built from cheaper sub-join paths.\n\n- **Phase 2 — Plan creation** (`createplan.c`): Once the optimizer selects the best Path (cheapest cost for the desired `tuple_fraction`), `create_plan()` recursively walks the Path tree and instantiates concrete `Plan` nodes. Plan nodes are executor-facing structures that reference Vars by relation-column offsets rather than catalog OIDs.\n\n**5. Hook Architecture**\nThe pipeline has hook points at every major stage: `post_parse_analyze_hook`, `planner_hook`, `set_rel_pathlist_hook`, `join_search_hook`, `create_upper_paths_hook`, `ExecutorStart_hook`, `ExecutorRun_hook`, `ExecutorFinish_hook`, `ExecutorEnd_hook`. These allow extensions (pg_stat_statements, auto_explain, custom access methods) to intercept and augment each stage without modifying core code.\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Input | Output | Key Responsibility |\n|-----------|-------|--------|--------------------|\n| `parser.c` + `scan.l` + `gram.y` | SQL string | `List<RawStmt>` | Lexing and grammar; no catalog access |\n| `analyze.c` | `RawStmt` | `Query` | Name resolution, type checking, semantic validation |\n| `rewriteHandler.c` | `Query` | `List<Query>` | View expansion, rule application, RLS |\n| `planner.c` / `allpaths.c` | `Query` | `Path` tree | Cost-based optimization, path enumeration |\n| `createplan.c` | `Path` | `Plan` tree | Path → executor-ready Plan conversion |\n| `execMain.c` | `PlannedStmt` | tuples | Executor lifecycle management |\n| `execProcnode.c` | `Plan` / `PlanState` | `TupleTableSlot` | Volcano dispatch |\n\n### Data Flow / Type Transformations\n\n```\nSQL string (const char*)\n    ↓ raw_parser() [parser.c + scan.l + gram.y]\nList<RawStmt>          — raw AST, no semantic content\n    ↓ parse_analyze_fixedparams() [analyze.c]\nQuery                  — semantic query tree: rtable, jointree, targetList, qualifications\n    ↓ QueryRewrite() [rewriteHandler.c]\nList<Query>            — post-rewrite queries (views expanded, rules applied)\n    ↓ planner() [planner.c] → make_one_rel() [allpaths.c]  [Phase 1]\nRelOptInfo with Path list — cost-annotated access strategy alternatives\n    ↓ create_plan() [createplan.c]                          [Phase 2]\nPlannedStmt { Plan *planTree } — executable plan tree\n    ↓ ExecutorStart() [execMain.c] → ExecInitNode() [execProcnode.c]\nPlanState tree         — runtime state parallel to Plan tree\n    ↓ ExecutorRun() → ExecutePlan() → ExecProcNode() loop [execProcnode.c]\nTupleTableSlot*        — one tuple per call (NULL = done)\n    ↓ DestReceiver.receiveSlot()\nClient result rows\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n- `RawStmt` has no OID references; it is safe to construct without catalog access\n- `Query` holds table/column names resolved to `Var` nodes with `varno` (range table index) and `varattno` (attribute number)\n- `PlannedStmt.planTree` is a tree of `Plan` nodes where all Vars are resolved to executor attribute numbers via `setrefs.c`\n- `PlanState` nodes are allocated 1:1 with `Plan` nodes and hold mutable execution state (current tuple, scan state, hash table, etc.)\n- `TupleTableSlot` is a fixed-size descriptor pointing to either a heap tuple or a virtual tuple of Datums; returned by reference and valid only until the next `ExecProcNode()` call unless explicitly copied\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL's query execution pipeline transforms a SQL string through five distinct stages: (1) **Parsing** (`parser.c`/`scan.l`/`gram.y`) produces a raw AST (`RawStmt`) with no catalog access; (2) **Semantic analysis** (`analyze.c`) resolves names and types to produce a `Query` node; (3) **Rewriting** (`rewriteHandler.c`) expands views and applies rules, yielding a `List<Query>`; (4) **Optimization** uses a two-phase process — path enumeration (`allpaths.c`) explores all access strategies with cost estimation, then `create_plan()` (`createplan.c`) converts the cheapest `Path` tree into an executable `PlannedStmt`; (5) **Execution** (`execMain.c`, `execProcnode.c`) uses the Volcano iterator model where `ExecProcNode()` dispatches via a per-node function pointer to node-specific handlers that recursively pull tuples from child nodes until `NULL` signals end-of-stream. The entire pipeline is extensible via hook points at each stage boundary.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
